**Executing SQL:**

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'))) - julianday(MIN(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp')))) * 86400.0 AS time_taken,
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') = 'tool-call')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.messages_json IS NOT NULL
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
)
SELECT * FROM thread_stats LIMIT 5;
```


**Results (5 rows):**

|--------------------------------------|-----------------|--------------|-------------------|

| 008bb75d-19af-42a6-96a7-62a059b91d13 | gpt-5.3-codex   |       55.588 |                 6 |
| 0093b144-668e-4615-b11c-b453a9f2de8e | claude-opus-4-6 |       29.265 |                 8 |

**Executing SQL:**

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'))) - julianday(MIN(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp')))) * 86400.0 AS time_taken,
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') = 'tool-call')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.messages_json IS NOT NULL
    AND t.database_name != 'threads'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
)
SELECT 
  model_name,
  AVG(time_taken) AS mean_time_taken,
  SQRT(AVG(time_taken * time_taken) - AVG(time_taken) * AVG(time_taken)) AS stddev_time_taken,
  AVG(tool_call_count) AS mean_tool_calls,
  SQRT(AVG(tool_call_count * tool_call_count) - AVG(tool_call_count) * AVG(tool_call_count)) AS stddev_tool_calls,
  COUNT(*) as thread_count
FROM thread_stats
GROUP BY model_name;
```


**Results (3 rows):**

| model_name             | mean_time_taken   | stddev_time_taken   |   mean_tool_calls |   stddev_tool_calls |   thread_count |
|------------------------|-------------------|---------------------|-------------------|---------------------|----------------|
| claude-opus-4-6        |                   |                     |                 0 |                   0 |            144 |
| gemini-3.1-pro-preview |                   |                     |                 0 |                   0 |            145 |
| gpt-5.3-codex          |                   |                     |                 0 |                   0 |            145 |

```sql
    ) AS tool_call_count
```

```sql
SELECT
  model_name,
  AVG(time_taken) AS mean_time_taken,
  COUNT(*) as thread_count
FROM (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'))) - julianday(MIN(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp')))) * 86400.0 AS time_taken
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.database_name != 'threads'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
)
GROUP BY model_name;
```

```sql
  time_taken
FROM (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'))) - julianday(MIN(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp')))) * 86400.0 AS time_taken
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
```

**Executing SQL:**

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"'))) - julianday(MIN(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"')))) * 86400.0 AS 
time_taken,
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') = 'tool-call')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.messages_json IS NOT NULL
    AND t.database_name != 'threads'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
)
SELECT 
  model_name,
  AVG(time_taken) AS mean_time_taken,
  SQRT(AVG(time_taken * time_taken) - AVG(time_taken) * AVG(time_taken)) AS stddev_time_taken,
  AVG(tool_call_count) AS mean_tool_calls,
  SQRT(AVG(tool_call_count * tool_call_count) - AVG(tool_call_count) * AVG(tool_call_count)) AS stddev_tool_calls,
  COUNT(*) as thread_count
FROM thread_stats
GROUP BY model_name;
```


**Results (3 rows):**

| model_name             |   mean_time_taken |   stddev_time_taken |   mean_tool_calls |   stddev_tool_calls |   thread_count |
|------------------------|-------------------|---------------------|-------------------|---------------------|----------------|
| claude-opus-4-6        |           18.594  |             12.8255 |                 0 |                   0 |            144 |
| gemini-3.1-pro-preview |           69.1181 |             69.1288 |                 0 |                   0 |            145 |
| gpt-5.3-codex          |           50.1828 |            168.644  |                 0 |                   0 |            145 |


**Executing SQL:**

```sql

      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') = 'tool-call')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.id = '003968ea-93bf-495b-829b-8dac9490ba55'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
```

**Executing SQL:**

```sql
SELECT
  SUM(
    (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') = 'tool-call')
  ) AS tool_call_count
FROM threads t
JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
WHERE t.id = '003968ea-93bf-495b-829b-8dac9490ba55';
```


**Results (1 rows):**

|-------------------|
|                 0 |


**Executing SQL:**

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'))) - julianday(MIN(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp')))) * 86400.0 AS time_taken,
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') = 'tool-call')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.id = '003968ea-93bf-495b-829b-8dac9490ba55'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
)
SELECT * FROM thread_stats;
```


**Results (1 rows):**

| id                                   | model_name    | time_taken   |   tool_call_count |
|--------------------------------------|---------------|--------------|-------------------|
| 003968ea-93bf-495b-829b-8dac9490ba55 | gpt-5.3-codex |              |                 0 |


**Executing SQL:**

```sql
SELECT
  SUM(
    CASE 
      WHEN json_type(m.value, '$.parts') = 'array' 
      THEN (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') = 'tool-call')
      ELSE 0 
    END
  ) AS tool_call_count
FROM threads t
JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
WHERE t.id = '003968ea-93bf-495b-829b-8dac9490ba55';
```


**Results (1 rows):**

|   tool_call_count |
|-------------------|
|                 0 |

```sql
FROM threads t, json_each(t.messages_json) m, json_each(m.value, '$.parts') p
WHERE t.id = '003968ea-93bf-495b-829b-8dac9490ba55'
```

**Executing SQL:**

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"'))) - julianday(MIN(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"')))) * 86400.0 AS 
time_taken,
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') LIKE '%tool-call%')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.messages_json IS NOT NULL
    AND t.database_name != 'threads'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
)
SELECT 
  model_name,
  AVG(time_taken) AS mean_time_taken,
  SQRT(AVG(time_taken * time_taken) - AVG(time_taken) * AVG(time_taken)) AS stddev_time_taken,
  AVG(tool_call_count) AS mean_tool_calls,
  SQRT(AVG(tool_call_count * tool_call_count) - AVG(tool_call_count) * AVG(tool_call_count)) AS stddev_tool_calls,
  COUNT(*) as thread_count
FROM thread_stats
GROUP BY model_name;
```


**Results (3 rows):**

| model_name             |   mean_time_taken |   stddev_time_taken |   mean_tool_calls |   stddev_tool_calls |   thread_count |
|------------------------|-------------------|---------------------|-------------------|---------------------|----------------|
| claude-opus-4-6        |           18.594  |             12.8255 |           6.40278 |             2.31637 |            144 |
| gemini-3.1-pro-preview |           69.1181 |             69.1288 |           9.85517 |             5.26796 |            145 |
| gpt-5.3-codex          |           50.1828 |            168.644  |           6.82069 |             2.08994 |            145 |

|          2 |

**Assistant:**

<analysis>
- **Core Question**: The user wants to calculate the average and standard deviation for the time taken to complete each thread ("call") and the number
of tool calls made within those threads, broken down by model.
- **Key Constraints**: 
  - Do not use the raw `created_at` and `ended_at` columns. Instead, parse the JSON in the `messages_json` column to get accurate timestamps.
  - Filter out records where the `database` column is "threads".
- **Data Entities**: 
  - `threads` table: contains `id`, `model_name`, `database_name`, and `messages_json`.
  - `messages_json`: a JSON array of message objects, each containing a `timestamp` and a nested `parts` array which includes `part_kind` attributes.
- **Data Exploration Plan**:
  1. Identify the structure of the `threads` table and sample the `messages_json` payload.
  2. Write an extraction query to compute the time difference (max timestamp - min timestamp) for each thread by unnesting `messages_json`.
  3. Write a subquery to count the number of tool calls per thread by extracting `part_kind = 'tool-call'`.
  4. Aggregate these derived metrics at the `model_name` level, calculating the mean and standard deviation (using the mathematical formula 
`SQRT(AVG(x^2) - AVG(x)^2)` since SQLite lacks a native `STDDEV` function).
- **Challenges & Edge Cases**: 
  - `json_extract` sometimes returns JSON string literals with double-quotes (e.g., `"2026-03-12..."`), which breaks timestamp conversion if not 
cleaned. We must strip the quotes.
  - The nested JSON arrays (`parts`) must be queried safely, returning 0 if there are no tool calls instead of nullifying the thread's row.
  - Standard deviation must be calculated manually.
</analysis>

I have explored the `threads` table and parsed the `messages_json` column to calculate the exact time spent and the number of tool calls per 
interaction. 

To achieve this, I used a query that unwraps the JSON, finds the minimum and maximum timestamps to determine the true duration in seconds, and counts 
how many times a `tool-call` part appears. I also applied the mathematical formula for Standard Deviation (`SQRT(AVG(x²) - AVG(x)²)`) since SQLite 
does not have a native standard deviation function, and filtered out any runs where the database was set to `"threads"`.

Here are the statistics (Mean and Standard Deviation) broken down by model:

### **Time Taken (in seconds)**
| Model | Mean Time Taken | Std Dev |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **claude-opus-4-6** | 18.59 s | 12.83 s |
| **gpt-5.3-codex** | 50.18 s | 168.64 s |
| **gemini-3.1-pro-preview** | 69.12 s | 69.13 s |

*Note: The high standard deviation for GPT-5.3 Codex indicates that while its average is around 50 seconds, there are some extreme outlier threads (I 
saw one in the dataset taking over 2,000 seconds) skewing the variance.*

### **Number of Tool Calls**
| Model | Mean Tool Calls | Std Dev |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **claude-opus-4-6** | 6.40 calls | 2.32 |
| **gpt-5.3-codex** | 6.82 calls | 2.09 |
| **gemini-3.1-pro-preview** | 9.86 calls | 5.27 |

### **Query Used**
For your reference, here is the SQL query that calculates these statistics from the raw JSON payload:

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    -- Calculate time taken in seconds using max and min timestamps inside the JSON
    (julianday(MAX(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"'))) - 
     julianday(MIN(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"')))) * 86400.0 AS time_taken,
    -- Count the occurrences of "tool-call" within the messages' parts array
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) 
       FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p 
       WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') LIKE '%tool-call%')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.messages_json IS NOT NULL
    AND t.database_name != 'threads'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
)
SELECT 
  model_name,
  AVG(time_taken) AS mean_time_taken,
  SQRT(AVG(time_taken * time_taken) - AVG(time_taken) * AVG(time_taken)) AS stddev_time_taken,
  AVG(tool_call_count) AS mean_tool_calls,
  SQRT(AVG(tool_call_count * tool_call_count) - AVG(tool_call_count) * AVG(tool_call_count)) AS stddev_tool_calls,
  COUNT(*) as thread_count
FROM thread_stats
GROUP BY model_name;
```


**User:**

Can you calculate median values any any other stats that would be useful


**Executing SQL:**

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"'))) - julianday(MIN(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"')))) * 86400.0 AS 
time_taken,
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') LIKE '%tool-call%')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.messages_json IS NOT NULL
    AND t.database_name != 'threads'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
),
ranked_stats AS (
  SELECT
    model_name,
    time_taken,
    tool_call_count,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY model_name ORDER BY time_taken) as rank_time,
    ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY model_name ORDER BY tool_call_count) as rank_tool,
    COUNT(*) OVER (PARTITION BY model_name) as cnt
  FROM thread_stats
)
SELECT 
  model_name,
  MIN(time_taken) AS min_time_taken,
  MAX(time_taken) AS max_time_taken,
  (
    SELECT AVG(time_taken)
    FROM ranked_stats r2
    WHERE r2.model_name = r1.model_name
      AND r2.rank_time IN (cnt/2, cnt/2 + 1, (cnt+1)/2)
  ) AS median_time_taken,
  MIN(tool_call_count) AS min_tool_calls,
  MAX(tool_call_count) AS max_tool_calls,
  (
    SELECT AVG(tool_call_count)
    FROM ranked_stats r2
    WHERE r2.model_name = r1.model_name
      AND r2.rank_tool IN (cnt/2, cnt/2 + 1, (cnt+1)/2)
  ) AS median_tool_calls
FROM ranked_stats r1
GROUP BY model_name;
```


**Results (3 rows):**

| model_name             |   min_time_taken |   max_time_taken |   median_time_taken |   min_tool_calls |   max_tool_calls |   median_tool_calls |
|------------------------|------------------|------------------|---------------------|------------------|------------------|---------------------|
| claude-opus-4-6        |           10.46  |          136.021 |             16.0135 |                4 |               27 |                   6 |
| gemini-3.1-pro-preview |           19.896 |          550.801 |             46.555  |                4 |               31 |                   8 |
| gpt-5.3-codex          |           14.101 |         2065.34  |             31.677  |                3 |               14 |                   6 |


**Executing SQL:**

```sql
WITH thread_stats AS (
  SELECT
    t.id,
    t.model_name,
    (julianday(MAX(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"'))) - julianday(MIN(TRIM(json_extract(m.value, '$.timestamp'), '"')))) * 86400.0 AS 
time_taken,
    SUM(
      (SELECT count(*) FROM json_each(m.value, '$.parts') AS p WHERE json_extract(p.value, '$.part_kind') LIKE '%tool-call%')
    ) AS tool_call_count
  FROM threads t
  JOIN json_each(t.messages_json) m
  WHERE t.messages_json IS NOT NULL
    AND t.database_name != 'threads'
  GROUP BY t.id, t.model_name
),
ranked_stats AS (
  SELECT
    model_name,
    time_taken,
    tool_call_count,
    NTILE(4) OVER (PARTITION BY model_name ORDER BY time_taken) as quartile_time,
    NTILE(4) OVER (PARTITION BY model_name ORDER BY tool_call_count) as quartile_tool
  FROM thread_stats
)
SELECT 
  model_name,
  MAX(CASE WHEN quartile_time = 1 THEN time_taken END) as p25_time,
  MAX(CASE WHEN quartile_time = 3 THEN time_taken END) as p75_time,
  MAX(CASE WHEN quartile_tool = 1 THEN tool_call_count END) as p25_tool,
  MAX(CASE WHEN quartile_tool = 3 THEN tool_call_count END) as p75_tool
FROM ranked_stats
GROUP BY model_name;
```


**Results (3 rows):**

| model_name             |   p25_time |   p75_time |   p25_tool |   p75_tool |
|------------------------|------------|------------|------------|------------|
| claude-opus-4-6        |     13.903 |     18.728 |          5 |          7 |
| gemini-3.1-pro-preview |     35.649 |     82.607 |          7 |         12 |
| gpt-5.3-codex          |     25.579 |     40.723 |          5 |          8 |

**Assistant:**

<analysis>
- **Core Question**: Calculate the median values and other useful statistics (like min, max, percentiles/quartiles) for the time taken and number of 
tool calls per model, ignoring the "threads" database.
- **Key Constraints**: Same as before, parse the JSON to compute the correct time_taken and tool_calls, ignoring `database_name = 'threads'`. SQLite 
lacks native median or percentile functions, so I must compute them using window functions (`ROW_NUMBER()` or `NTILE()`).
- **Data Exploration Plan**:
  1. Re-run the core extraction CTE (`thread_stats`) to get `id`, `model_name`, `time_taken`, and `tool_call_count` for each thread.
  2. Use a second CTE (`ranked_stats`) with window functions:
     - `ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY model_name ORDER BY ...)` to find the middle rows for the median.
     - `NTILE(4)` to find the 25th (P25) and 75th (P75) percentiles (quartiles).
  3. Aggregate the min, max, median, 25th percentile, and 75th percentile for both metrics grouped by model.
- **Challenges**: SQLite requires subqueries or self-joins to extract the specific middle rows for the exact median, and `NTILE(4)` to fetch 
quartiles.
</analysis>

I've calculated a broader set of statistics to give you a clearer picture of the distribution, as averages can often be skewed by extreme outliers 
(which we saw earlier with `gpt-5.3-codex`).

Here are the detailed statistics including Median, Min, Max, and the 25th/75th Percentiles (which help show where the "middle 50%" of the data lives).

### **Time Taken (in seconds)**
| Model | Min | 25th Percentile | **Median** | 75th Percentile | Max |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **claude-opus-4-6** | 10.46 s | 13.90 s | **16.01 s** | 18.73 s | 136.02 s |
| **gpt-5.3-codex** | 14.10 s | 25.58 s | **31.68 s** | 40.72 s | 2065.34 s |
| **gemini-3.1-pro-preview** | 19.90 s | 35.65 s | **46.56 s** | 82.61 s | 550.80 s |

**Insights on Time:** 
Looking at the median, `claude-opus-4-6` is significantly faster on a typical task (16 seconds vs ~32 and ~47 seconds). Notice how `gpt-5.3-codex` has
a median of ~31.7 seconds, but its average (from earlier) was ~50 seconds—this proves that a few incredibly long tasks (like the 2,065 second max) 
were heavily dragging its average up.

### **Number of Tool Calls**
| Model | Min | 25th Percentile | **Median** | 75th Percentile | Max |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **claude-opus-4-6** | 4 calls | 5 calls | **6 calls** | 7 calls | 27 calls |
| **gpt-5.3-codex** | 3 calls | 5 calls | **6 calls** | 8 calls | 14 calls |
| **gemini-3.1-pro-preview** | 4 calls | 7 calls | **8 calls** | 12 calls | 31 calls |

**Insights on Tool Calls:**
`claude-opus-4-6` and `gpt-5.3-codex` are highly efficient, typically solving the problem in exactly 6 tool calls. `gemini-3.1-pro-preview` tends to 
take a bit more exploration, generally utilizing 8 tool calls for a typical task, and having a wider spread (with its middle 50% falling between 7 and
12 calls).
